# Air Quality Sensor Calibration | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Verkada [Air Quality Sensors](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 have an assortment of different readings that allow you to gain more insight into your building or monitor areas where video monitoring is not allowed. The data available depends on the model of the sensor.

You can use Verkada sensors to monitor temperature, humidity, carbon dioxide, and other environmental conditions throughout indoor spaces to identify possible impacts on human health or asset performance.

The Verkada Air Quality Sensor calibration interface:

*   Allows you to calibrate your sensors to your specification needs and easily download a certificate to verify compliance.
    
*   Provides another level of actionability and verification to the rich data collected by Verkada sensors.
    

Our sensors are factory-calibrated and rated to the specified

accuracy in the [SV20 Series Air Quality Sensor](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 overview

for a minimum of 10 years.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#calibrate-a-verkada-sensor)

Calibrate a Verkada sensor


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The temperature and humidity sensors onboard the [SV20 Series](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 and [SV11](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/sensors-quick-start-guide.pdf)
 sensors are individually tested and calibrated. To ensure their continued accuracy, recalibration (using an external reference device) is necessary.

For the calibration, Verkada uses transfer standards, which are subject to a scheduled calibration procedure. The calibration of the reference, used for the calibration of the transfer standards, is [National Institute of Standards and Technology](https://www.nist.gov/)
 (NIST)-traceable through an [ISO/IEC 17025](https://www.iso.org/ISO-IEC-17025-testing-and-calibration-laboratories.html)
 accredited laboratory.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#enable-sensor-calibration-globally)

Enable sensor calibration globally

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin.**

2

**In the left navigation, select Privacy & Security .**

3

**Select Feature Manager.**

4

**On Air Quality > Sensor Calibration, select Enable.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-89759f19589546238f17a003c514fc6172c5501f%252Fba361bfdfd24d75b1f41609bfca8db092033b9fc.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=12d8d761&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#view-sensor-calibration-data)

View sensor calibration data

1

**In Command, go to All Products > Air Quality .**

2

**On the left navigation, click Calibration .**

3

**On Sensor Calibration, select the reading you want to calibrate.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-05c6436fbf103a4ac019f11cfcf8be742bb307c0%252Fb603425b76341b989c259d4c27fa0263b91e2545.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9405229e&sv=2)

You should be able to see all of your devices, their site, calibration status, current reading if an offset has been applied, when and who updated it, and the next due date.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-571426cf7655f2f6966c59902e3cf160c724025e%252F947b6381138ad1c0b1f9032c1fef755db34ced9a.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9567e175&sv=2)

*   **Device Name**—Name of the device you want to calibrate.
    
*   **Site**—Location of the device you want to calibrate.
    
*   **Status**—Status of the device.
    
    *   **N/A**—No calibration has been applied.
        
    *   **Calibrated**—A calibration profile has been applied.
        
    *   **Past Due**—The calibration profile has expired.
        
    
*   **Current**—Current reading of the selected sensor reading.
    
*   **Offset**—Offset error that is applied in the calibration profile.
    
*   **Last Updated**—Date the sensor was calibrated.
    
*   **Updated By**—User who applied the calibration.
    
*   **Due Date**—Due date for the next calibration. The calibration procedure should be done on or before this date.
    

4

**Click the sensor device you want to calibrate.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-89d9a0ad6d167bea6b0c0f9706bd1c625468bab9%252F82dddcee8acc1c0ddfc8bd427b94c6aca3a33485.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=750d824a&sv=2)

5

**Using a reference device, take a reading while holding your reference device next to your sensor.** _**The closer you are to the sensor, the more accurate your calibration is**_**.**

a. Enter this reading in the **Reference Reading** field.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e8e9566b7ae4f0f608742262ffe218a7557356f8%252F298451fc97fefed78a6603e80e5aa1548a4ec176.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9111a2e8&sv=2)

b. If you see an "Offset exceeds range" warning, this means that the device is reading a value past its typical accuracy. We recommend that you check your reference device and ensure you have properly followed the installation guidelines.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-ff532cfe7ab4c52138ee1bc624ddbbe9bb84f4c1%252Fef7b33106ef70e6163bbfdce1dce7186cdd85610.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cddfa686&sv=2)

c. If you see the "Offset limit reached" warning, this means you’ve reached the offset limit for the reading. Either your reference device is wrong or your sensor may not be operating properly. For assistance, contact [Verkada Support](https://www.verkada.com/contact/)
.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-33b0d7a57bfeb38f0b8a567abe02e53e1ede2b70%252F5f2953f3662359d594837569f2505449d65787d5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=76f23f54&sv=2)

6

**Click Refresh immediately after taking your reference reading to get the current raw reading from your sensor.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c12b034765417541f13c3e52e91686defee9af94%252F60ecec65a8bfe902983f6e6110f046c20c23f36e.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b992d8be&sv=2)

7

**Review your calibration profile and click Next.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-47dc8cc2a99f3eb9e70a6a3e957a9c9a9ab6ff89%252Fb8ed55f082fa0ed247fbb3d73e7092e4f786e4b0.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2b986588&sv=2)

8

**(Optional) Check the Download Calibration Report box to download a PDF of your calibration report.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-46a29f60a47174ff12af50e1f54153e32e665f75%252Ff9fa9e145fe7ed67deb66899fdbf88b892936610.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=79995f24&sv=2)

9

**Click Apply to confirm your calibration.**

A calibration event is then permanently stored in the audit log and the offset is immediately applied to your sensor.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-d97fb55f40d3c8e403139f98934a2e9540c17139%252F2687b1bc8ec90d0a945a11bd731b8b747dcdc4f9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3cd4079a&sv=2)

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#download-the-most-recent-calibration-certificate)

Download the most recent calibration certificate


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You may need to download a calibration certificate to provide to a third party. You can do this done during the calibration process or you can retrieve it at a later date using the calibration page.

Your sensor must have previously been ​[calibrated](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_c18dfe453b)
 to download a calibration certificate.

When you download a calibration certificate, it creates an audit entry in the [org-wide audit log](https://help.verkada.com/command/organization-wide-settings/manage-and-view-audit-logs)
.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-98ef3e626e317e565e5beff6df871cd5e219bc65%252F04f65d6a1ca06dfa9ea67115987fcbd94c82883b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=acf3ec4e&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#how-it-works)

How it works

1

**From the calibration page, select a reading. As an example, look at a sensor’s Temperature calibration history.**

2

**Hover over the device and at the bottom right, find and click Download Calibration Report.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-5cd967c2825aa14dd8188d5fed3f5c5341db7612%252F86ba032d6aba03ca11838b4e572c8cd8d036c635.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c6fecd6b&sv=2)

3

**Command processes your request and a browser download of the calibration certificate will be initiated once the file is ready.**

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#view-calibration-history)

View calibration history


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Verkada stores all of the different calibration events and certificates, as the calibration history, for each device. This means that every action is permanently logged, when you:

*   Apply a calibration
    
*   [Reset a device](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_e5d297a428)
     to factory calibration settings
    

When you download a calibration certificate, it creates an audit entry in the [org-wide audit log](https://help.verkada.com/command/organization-wide-settings/manage-and-view-audit-logs)
.

1

**From the calibration page, select a reading. As an example, look at a sensor’s Temperature calibration history.**

2

**Hover over the device and at the bottom right, click the kebab menu (3 vertical dots).**

3

**Select View Calibration History.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-b3571b8fefc38e6ed5a72381f1bdae236e413a72%252F85bcc70449c9e37d22619bae32334ca7a689dd2e.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6eaf62cc&sv=2)

The history log shows the following:

*   What event took place (Factory Reset | Calibration)
    
*   The date when the event occurred
    
*   The offset that was applied
    
*   The reference reading that was taken during that calibration
    
*   The certificate number for that calibration
    
*   The user who made the change
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#download-calibration-reports)

Download calibration reports


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**Continue from how to** [**View calibration history**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_1caa74091c)
**.**

2

**Hover over the table row.**

3

**At the right, find the download arrow and click Download Calibration Report.**

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#reset-a-sensors-calibration-to-factory-defaults)

Reset a sensor’s calibration to factory defaults


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Command allows you to use the factory calibration settings or reset your sensor back to factory default settings if a calibration profile is no longer needed.

1

**Your sensor must be** [**calibrated**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_c18dfe453b)
 **to reset it to factory defaults.**

2

**When you reset a sensor back to factory calibration settings, it creates an entry in the sensor’s calibration history.**

1

**From the calibration page, select a reading. As an example, look at a sensor’s Temperature calibration history.**

2

**Hover over the device and at the bottom right, click the kebab menu (3 vertical dots).**

3

**Select Reset Factory Settings.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-82785feee82b041589ef7c9877d7b0eb64c72bb6%252Fe9936b63ccffb1f65cf4469c5dcaa7671b23c252.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ad07b2ec&sv=2)

4

**Click Reset to confirm to reset the factory settings for the specified device.**

*   If successful, you will see a "Factory calibration reset complete" banner.
    
*   If unsuccessful, contact [Verkada Support](https://www.verkada.com/contact/)
    .
    

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#faq)

FAQ


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Do I need to calibrate my sensor?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#do-i-need-to-calibrate-my-sensor)

Most customers do not need to calibrate their sensors.

However, you may be required to annually calibrate your devices. With the **Air Quality Sensor Calibration** page, you can now use a reference device to calibrate your sensors. Once calibrated, you can [download a PDF certificate](http://help.verkada.com/en/articles/7852972-air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_5729ad46fa)
 showing that your sensor was calibrated.

Which Verkada sensors can be calibrated?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#which-verkada-sensors-can-be-calibrated)

Follow the [calibrate an air quality sensor](http://help.verkada.com/en/articles/7852972-air-quality-sensor-calibration#h_c18dfe453b)
 steps to calibrate all Verkada sensors, including the last-generation [SV11](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/sensors-quick-start-guide.pdf)
s and the latest [SV20 Series](https://help.verkada.com/en/articles/6732870-what-s-new-in-the-sv20-series)
 sensors (SV21s, SV23s, SV25s).

What kind of calibration does Verkada offer?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#what-kind-of-calibration-does-verkada-offer)

Currently, the **Air Quality Sensor Calibration** page allows you to apply a standard one-point linear calibration to your sensors. Verkada uses a single point to calculate the difference between the reference value and the raw reading to create an offset correction for the error between the two, and then apply that offset to the sensor reading.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a70a33e8d83f0e0623f6ea6275d3ac657ae2b43d%252F89dc98f46f498f22d766c4afc025fcae90a87125.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9373b512&sv=2)

For example, if your sensor’s raw Temperature reading is 72˚F (22˚C), but your reference device shows 71˚F (21˚C), and your offset is – 1˚F. Once the calibration is applied, if your raw reading is 76˚F (24˚C), your sensor will show 75˚F (23˚C) in Command.

Who can calibrate a Verkada sensor?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#who-can-calibrate-a-verkada-sensor)

**Only Org Admins can calibrate Verkada sensors.** The Org Admin must also be a Site Admin for the sites in which the sensors are located. If the Org Admin doesn’t have Site Admin permissions, they can’t view the sensors. To understand role permissions, see [Detailed Role Breakdown for Command Users](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command)
.

Which sensor readings can be calibrated?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#which-sensor-readings-can-be-calibrated)

*   Temperature
    
*   Humidity
    
*   Carbon Dioxide
    
*   Carbon Monoxide
    
*   Noise Level
    
*   PM 2.5, 4.0, and 10.0
    

Does setting the calibration affect past data?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#does-setting-the-calibration-affect-past-data)

No, calibrating your devices does not affect the past data collected by your sensors. Only the data from the point of calibration onwards has the offset incorporated into it.

What kind of reference devices does Verkada recommend using?[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/air-quality-sensor-calibration#what-kind-of-reference-devices-does-verkada-recommend-using)

Verkada recommends using NIST Traceable Temperature/Humidity sensors, such as the _Traceable Barometric/Temperature/Humidity Wi-Fi Data Logger_ or the _Fluke - 52-260HZCAL 52-2 Dual Input Digital Thermometer with a NIST-Traceable Calibration Certificate with Data_ for calibrating your temperature or humidity sensors. Verkada recommends the _TSI DustTrak™ DRX 8533_ for PM 2.5, PM 4.0, and PM 10 calibration.

Last updated 22 hours ago

Was this helpful?

# Integrate Verkada Cameras with Air Quality Sensors | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Pair your Verkada Air Quality Sensor with a Verkada Camera to gain visual evidence into environmental conditions or events. Spot events, identify problematic areas or conditions, protect your people and assets—all on a single pane of glass.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/integrate-verkada-cameras-with-air-quality-sensors#add-a-camera-feed-to-your-air-quality-sensor)

Add a camera feed to your air quality sensor


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You may want to add a camera feed so that you can see what’s going on near the sensor at a quick glance.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Select a sensor where you want to add a camera feed.**

3

**At the top right, click the Camera icon.**

4

**Select which camera you want to add to this sensor.**

5

**Click Confirm > Done to add the camera.**

You should see the camera feed appear next to the sensor information.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/integrate-verkada-cameras-with-air-quality-sensors#change-or-remove-a-camera-feed-from-a-sensor)

Change or remove a camera feed from a sensor


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Select a sensor where you want to change or remove a camera feed.**

3

**At the top right, click Edit Camera (pencil icon).**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-7351155b1162481a04808d2990390b3bb22741d9%252F7aa2db0f278f90cdb85c41aaddd9f6cc6cfb9f94.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fa168d94&sv=2)

4

**On Select Camera, change which camera is selected.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-7b2c84ad9634820fbbf9ebbb1ea85909e0df5ee7%252F9f6f5a49be474f97312a144eb10b3c1133be543d.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=f7787bbf&sv=2)

5

**(Optional) On Edit Settings > Camera, remove the feed completely:**

a. Click the **Settings** (gear) icon. b. Click **Remove Camera**.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-eefbd75462bc92c811114b01f805f05b982fa43c%252F372da219e8d66119abc43e72056be409a34cc44e.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c7b7586e&sv=2)

6

**Click Apply to finalize the settings.**

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/integrate-verkada-cameras-with-air-quality-sensors#camera-and-sensor-graph-overlay-view)

Camera and sensor graph overlay view


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality .**

2

**Select a sensor to view.**

3

**At the top right, click to change views.**

4

**You should see the sensor graph overlayed on top of the camera feed with sensor events listed on the right. The events are scrollable and may be filtered by date, time, and/or sensor reading.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-ff0d62a6e34abc288a46a4b34c86f56c8f6e6338%252F24ca34cf88fab02b4fea796a874a7b787377997b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b3bcd221&sv=2)

5

**Hover over the camera feed and click to access the sensor graph and camera overlay mode in full-screen mode.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-2142f0485b7b129e4057d499592f599fe6832eb2%252F8ef4fcf33029d9b45c240202f68b359f9a496b9b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=7da7c583&sv=2)

The ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a8470e2d5d3e2d2bdf1c7dd44572f9422814f622%252F16211ea8294bbc9508520d83b7a63923f52dbe80.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d880001b&sv=2) button will take you to the camera history player, where you can archive footage.

# Air Quality Event Analytics | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Verkada’s [air quality sensors](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 are designed to give you the ability to monitor environments for abnormal conditions automatically and in real time. With sensor analytics, you can track and monitor alert trends, environmental trends, and behaviors across your organization, at the site and device levels.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-event-analytics#access-event-analytics)

Access event analytics


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The **Event Analytics** page makes it easier to view and analyze your sensor data. You can now specify which readings to evaluate to see how many alerts are generated on a daily, weekly, or monthly basis. The page has an easy-to-use graph to help identify trends and a table to show the count of total alerts and associated changes.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**On the left navigation, click Analytics .**

3

**On Event Analytics:**

a. Click the sensor reading dropdown and choose which reading you want to view. You can select from any of the [Air Quality sensor readings](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
 available; however, only alerts on configured and supported devices contribute to the data. b. Click the **timeframe** dropdown (by default, **Weekly** is selected) and choose which timeframe you want to view.

*   **Hourly**—Shows an hour-by-hour view of the selected day.
    
*   **Daily**—Shows a day-by-day view of the past 12 days.
    
*   **Weekly**—Shows a week-by-week view for the past 12 weeks.
    
*   **Monthly**—Shows a month-by-month view for the past 12 months.
    

g. Click the **sites** dropdown (by default, **All Sites** is selected), and individually select the sites you want to review. If you’re only interested in a portion of the devices in the sites, we recommend that you create a new subsite for those devices.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-event-analytics#understand-the-analytics-table)

Understand the analytics table

Within the detailed view:

*   You see a breakdown of how your selected sites have performed over the time interval selected compared to their previous performance.
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-7e60e07754aff8a999a33fe5bb9ec81da79f2e58%252F2ee5b828eb51c8effd08cb0ffcc600c8e00402bf.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9b668bea&sv=2)
    
*   At the top left, you see a composite summary of the reading for all selected sites over the time interval selected. You may also select a new sensor reading to analyze.
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-aa947f8c319be8e8b46df9c8763164b745e4bbc3%252Fb45b82a0489e75d6b7dc0aa119dae372eded0233.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b06b023b&sv=2)
    
*   You can select any of the columns to be the active tab.
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f7ca3c0b183326f34760df66ab2a0526a8c643a7%252Fea0d1875cc62f5bc8ac16e3e60b1519bde9f3ef6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=36773495&sv=2)
    
*   **Totals Alerts** show the sum of all alerts over the time interval selected.
    
    *   The number above the column and in the summary section on the top left of the page is the total sum of the **Totals Alerts** for all sites.
        
    
*   **Change** shows the change as a percentage-based reference over the time interval selected.
    
    *   A **red upward arrow** indicates an uptick in alerts over the measured period.
        
    *   A **green downward arrow** indicates a decrease in alerts over the measured period.
        
    *   No change over time is expressed as **0%**.
        
    *   An increase from zero events in the reference column is considered undefined (division by zero) and is expressed as **–%**.
        
    *   The most alerts can increase over time is infinite with a **2x increase** corresponding to a **100% change**.
        
    *   The most alerts can decrease over time is finite converging to 0% where a **2x decrease** corresponds to a **50% change**.
        
    

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-b56a5da9b23a8de3d5c3ab83b232cfef83dfd975%252F9c12fac276533900904e253ed2b605f999d58e99.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=17bac57c&sv=2)

# Audio Recording with the SV25 | Air Quality | Verkada Help

The Verkada [SV25](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 Air Quality Sensor has audio recording capability that provides up to **365** days of audio recording on SV25s where you can easily review, save, and download audio clips directly from Verkada Command.

**Model (SKU)**

**Audio Retention**

**Storage**

SV25

**90 Days**

32 GB

SV25-128

**365 Days**

128 GB

Audio recording pairs natively with the other sensor readings on the SV25 and Verkada cameras and other devices, giving important context into your environment.

With audio recording, SV25 you can protect, monitor, and manage your environments across a range of use cases, including:

*   Adding audio context and verification to noise and motion alerts
    
*   As a tool to comply with state regulations that require audio recording in specific school settings
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/audio-recording-with-the-sv25#enable-audio-recording)

Enable audio recording


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Org Admins want visibility and control over which devices make use of audio recording. To help address these needs, Verkada has implemented processes to help ensure that audio recording is deployed in a way that respects individual privacy.

By default, all audio recording capabilities are **disabled on all SV25 units**. This means that no SV25 records audio out of the box. Only Org Admins can enable the feature.

1

**Admins must review and accept a set of Terms and Conditions from within the Privacy and Security page within Command.**

2

**Once the Terms and Conditions have been accepted, Org Admins need to enable audio on a per-device level. This ensures that audio recording is enabled only on an as-needed basis.**

3

**Org Admins can also choose between "live only audio" (no audio is recorded) or "live and recorded audio" (up to 365 days of audio is recorded on the device and is available in Verkada Command).**

4

**There is a ‘kill switch’ available at the Organization level. This switch allows Org Admins to disable audio recording on all sensors with the flip of a switch. The control also deletes any audio already recorded on any SV25 device.**

5

**The data ownership, responsibility, and authorization for the use of audio recording is at the sole discretion of the customer.**

Audio recordings are stored on the device, not in the cloud, and can be downloaded from the device through Command when needed for investigations.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/audio-recording-with-the-sv25#enable-audio-per-device)

Enable audio per device


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

These options are only available if the org-level permissions and Terms and Conditions have been set and accepted.

1

**Under the SV25 settings menu, or when multiple SV25s are selected for bulk editing, you should see the Audio tab with the option to enable Live Audio and Recorded Audio.**

​**Note**: To have recorded audio work, you must also have live audio enabled. ​

2

**Once these settings are confirmed, the device refreshes and sensor readings are unavailable for about 10 seconds. The device is always expected to refresh if either of these settings is changed.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-91b4bba4c3e124a5d433ab481ad10854a635e360%252Fa78d23fde90d4aac8c154de63b336f5838315e3e.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=af1a047c&sv=2)

3

**The device should now have an Audio pill at the bottom of the list of enabled sensors. If only the live audio is enabled, you only see the option to view live audio and not historical.**

4

**If recorded audio is also enabled, you should be able to see the same navigation scrubber you are familiar with from other sensor readings.**

5

**Audio shows a waveform based on the detected noise level picked up from the noise level sensor, which is not capable of audio recording alone. Because of this, it is possible to see a waveform that reflects the noise level of the environment despite audio recording being turned off or a recorded segment being missing or unavailable.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-181d27fccb111e62baa85a862693fba73e22a87b%252F7f2cc94424b95cdb690a0fadda30e66552e85753.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=68ce254d&sv=2)

6

**You are now able to listen to historic audio by scrubbing to that time window and selecting it like any other sensor reading. The audio plays from that moment. The Verkada Command tab must remain active on your browser for audio to continue playing for both historic and live. Switching to another tab stops your audio playback.**

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/audio-recording-with-the-sv25#download-a-segment-of-audio)

Download a segment of audio


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When you download an audio segment, it is very different from a camera archive, as the requested portion of audio is never stored on the cloud, rather only emailed to you.

This means that deleting the email containing the past audio archives will mean that the archive is lost forever.

1

**On the audio service bar, click the Download icon. You should see a time selection download prompt.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-3313ae5feee3f0f7cd0c53c4661767dd74707e1d%252F6181ec73eb820914fc5c77606c85e840e2e17c1e.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ee1b99d&sv=2)

2

**Define the span of time and click Download to have a copy of that clip sent to your email.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-376c3c0cdf7270e7c0b6e901fe460ccce9f2ba93%252F6fb2ca94bba19e71fd181b4add9f763a5184c172.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=881cd3ca&sv=2)

For security reasons, the **Download** button does not allow the direct file to be downloaded.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/audio-recording-with-the-sv25#erase-audio)

Erase audio


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If for any reason you want to erase your recorded audio or disable the feature, you can set the **live** or **historical** option to disable from the SV25s device menu.

Last updated 19 hours ago

Was this helpful?

# Air Quality Alerts Migration | Air Quality | Verkada Help

On November 15, 2023, Verkada [Air Quality Sensor](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 customers will be migrated to a new alert experience.

You can now display and view your Verkada [Air Quality Sensor](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 alerts from the [**Alerts**](https://help.verkada.com/verkada-cameras/events-and-alerts/create-alerts-across-verkada-products)
 page in Verkada [Command](https://help.verkada.com/command/get-started-with-verkada-command)
, making it easier to manage all alerts from a single page across your Verkada products. You can also manage your alert workflows on the **Admin** > [**Manage Alerts**](https://help.verkada.com/verkada-cameras/events-and-alerts/manage-alerts-across-verkada-products)
 page.

This new feature expands alert functionality:

*   Org Admins can now enable push notifications for all sensor events, including vape, temperature, and more.
    
*   With push notifications, users can now use the Command mobile app to receive a notification straight to their mobile device.
    
*   Org Admins can now subscribe groups to a notification, and sensor alerts now have a Command user group, allowing for much easier alert-recipient management.
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#new-migration-process)

New migration process


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#alert-management)

Alert management

Prior to the new migration, alerts were managed on the sensor’s detail settings page:

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-5f0548102cffe0fb17b18821d9d44caa23382518%252Fc5205d18ab0900e770383e87111c09de6fbb4ef8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c91c2d31&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#alert-creation)

Alert creation

During the migration process, the new alert rules are created on a **per-user** basis.

The migration created one (1) alert rule for each user, for each of the following:

1

**One or more sensor alerts. Multiple readings and devices will be grouped together in this alert as a union.**

2

**One or more sensor zone events.**

3

**One or more sensor status events (offline alerts).**

In the previous alert system, sensor offline notifications were email only. Now you can receive SMS or Push notifications in addition to email.

This means that post-migration, you can have, **at most**, **3 alert rules** if you were subscribed to all 3 of the different use cases.

For each of these alerts, your previous sensor notification settings schedule was used for the schedule in the new alert system. This also includes the **Disable when alert ends** setting.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a3695d3f9917d59e59a7f2642cd3c704021b05f8%252F26a40fb2f86024b6087cf19a42f0ea365a7febb0.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=372b45d3&sv=2)

If the SMS method was enabled in the previous alert system, the **Push** notification method was automatically enabled in the new alert system.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#alert-name-format)

Alert name format

The alert name is generated using the following format and depends on the alert type:

*   User name’s sensor alerts
    
*   User name’s zone alerts
    
*   User name’s status alerts
    

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#editor-role)

Editor role

The new alert system introduces the role of **Editor**. Editors can see, modify, and delete their alerts.

*   In the previous alert system, all [Site Admins](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command)
     were Editors.
    
*   In the new alert system, all Site Admins who oversee devices where a user was subscribed are now added as an Editor.
    

Any **new** Site Admins are not automatically added as an Editor.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#how-this-new-alert-system-works)

How this new alert system works

At a high level, here are some helpful examples that show how this new alert system works:

*   If you have 10 users subscribed to vape alerts on 100 sensors, you would have 10 alert rules.
    
*   If you have 1 user subscribed to vape alerts on 100 sensors, you would have 1 alert rule.
    
*   If you have 2 users subscribed to vape alerts on 1 sensor, you would have 2 alert rules.
    
*   If you have 5 users subscribed to vape and temperature alerts on 10 sensors, you would have 5 alert rules.
    
*   If you had one user who was subscribed to sensor alerts, sensor zone alerts, and sensor offline alerts set up, they would have 3 alert rules:
    
    *   John Doe’s sensor alerts
        
    *   John Doe’s sensor zone alert
        
    *   John Doe’s sensor status alerts
        
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f10a6e3b01c5b91820b3f4664afa2188f779a0f7%252Fa32eaa51058d4b663fc9af2fb0f4c503df6a87cb.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=eaeef2dc&sv=2)
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a4ca38921b5757fa05477a772baca62aec01d13a%252F9bab6d09e1ccd227c58824c94f9215cb991c0ed3.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1a0a0737&sv=2)
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#user-journey-from-previous-to-current-alert-system)

User journey from previous to current alert system


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The goal of this topic is to take you through the pre and post-migration process.

1

**Explore how your alerts appeared in the** [**previous alerts system**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#h_8475fadc96)
**.**

2

**Explain how your alerts appear in the** [**new alert system**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#h_fc29f16609)
**.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#previous-alert-system-example)

Previous alert system (example)

In the previous system, where "Dominic" is the user with these details:

*   Subscribed to 3 sensors: vape, noise, and temperature alerts.
    
*   Scheduled from Monday through Friday, 8:00 AM to 6:30 PM (as shown below).
    
*   **Disabled when alert ends** disabled (meaning Dominic would receive a second notification when the alert ended).
    
*   In this example, there is another Site Admin ("Will") who can modify these devices.
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-929c2e825356bc09b98f26d259b1f98784b9b919%252F79ea19c5364299e217da024c38c21da766ff6aae.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9d0debb3&sv=2)
    
*   "Dominic" is also subscribed to one (1) device’s offline alerts:

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#new-alert-system-post-migration)

New alert system (post-migration)

In the new alert system, you can go to the [**Manage Alerts**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#h_38985b302d)
 page to see your migrated alerts.

#### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#manage-alerts-page)

Manage Alerts page

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin.**

2

**Under Org Settings, click Manage Alerts.**

3

**(Optional) At the top, you may need to click Shared Alerts to filter alerts.**

All migrated air quality sensor alerts are shared alerts.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-9180ae548978dd29cc1faecfe50ce0ac1e108979%252F0ed08a5a86fed1775121246e9a559686261bbc07.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=ac87260&sv=2)

 **rule—Contains any sensor device readings he was subscribed to. In this case, it was 3 sensors and he was subscribed to the vape, noise, and tamper sensor readings.**

2

[**Dominic’s status alerts**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#h_523b84ebac)
 **rule—Contains any sensor offline alerts he was subscribed to. In this case, it was one sensor.**

3

[**Dominic’s zone alerts**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-alerts-migration#h_4f1c9fe5ab)
 **rule—Contains any sensor zones he was subscribed to. In this case, it was 1 sensor zone. Previously, sensor zones would alert to all readings. This means that all sensor readings are selected during the migration process.**

# Roles and Permissions for Command | Command | Verkada Help

This article describes the set of roles and associated permissions for [Verkada Command](https://help.verkada.com/command/get-started-with-verkada-command)
.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#roles-and-permissions-by-verkada-product)

Roles and permissions by Verkada product

All users added to the organization can log in to Command but need additional permissions to view all the products. Select a product from the list below for more information on its roles and permissions.

*   [Roles and Permissions for Access Control](https://help.verkada.com/access-control/roles-and-permissions-for-access-control)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Air Quality Sensors](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/roles-and-permissions-for-air-quality-sensors)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Alarms](https://help.verkada.com/new-alarms/roles-and-permissions-for-new-alarms)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Classic Alarms](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/roles-and-permissions-for-classic-alarms)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Cameras](https://help.verkada.com/verkada-cameras/configuration-and-setup/roles-and-permissions-for-cameras)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Intercom](https://help.verkada.com/intercom/roles-and-permissions-for-intercom)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Gateway](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/roles-and-permissions-for-gateway)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Guest](https://intercom.help/verkada/en/articles/5715499-roles-and-permissions-for-guest)
    
*   [Roles and Permissions for Mailroom](https://help.verkada.com/mailroom/roles-and-permissions-for-mailroom)
    

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#organization-level-roles)

Organization-level roles


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Organization member[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#organization-member)

All users added to an organization are organization members. A user added to the organization who does not have admin permissions has the minimum level of access needed to sign in to the organization.

Access allows you to:

*   View the organization when logged in.
    
*   Configure personal notifications (which alerts the user wants to receive).
    
*   Set personal 2-Factor Authentication (2FA) settings.
    

Command User Admin[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#command-user-admin)

Any organization member can be upgraded to a Command User Admin.

Access allows you to:

*   Add and remove users, designate their roles, and assign them to groups.
    
*   Add and remove groups and assign users to groups.
    
*   Add and remove contacts for individuals outside of your organization.
    
*   Create and assign alerts to groups and users in the organization.
    
*   Manage and restrict access to Shared Links for users in the organization.
    
*   Enable Support Access.
    

Organization Admin[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#organization-admin)

Any organization member can be upgraded to an Organization Admin.

Access allows you to:

*   View the organization when logged in.
    
*   Configure personal notifications (which alerts the user wants to receive).
    
*   Set personal and org-wide 2FA settings.
    
*   Create floor plans.
    
*   Add, delete, and modify access users.
    
*   Set user and group permissions for the organization and all sites/subsites.
    
*   Configure org-wide settings, including maximum archive duration, enable/disable cloud backup globally, and default camera playback quality.
    
*   Rename or delete the org.
    
*   Create new sites and subsites.
    
*   Add and remove devices.
    
*   Adjust camera stream encoding settings.
    

If the [Global Site Admin](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/customize-roles-and-permissions)
 policy is enabled, all Org Admins will automatically be granted Site Admin access to all sites.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#set-permissions)

Set permissions


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Command User Admin[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#command-user-admin-1)

**Grant permissions**

In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin .Under Admin > Users & Permissions, click Users.Select a user to grant permissions.Next to Command Roles click .a. Select Command User Admin. b. Click Apply Changes.

**Revoke permissions**

In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin .Under Admin > Users & Permissions, click Users.Select a user to grant permissions.Next to Command Roles click .a. Select None. b. Click Apply Changes.

Command User Admins cannot modify the Organization Admin role. They can assign or remove Command User Admins but cannot elevate or lower Organization Admin permissions.

Organization Admin[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#organization-admin-1)

**Grant permissions**

In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin .Under Admin > Users & Permissions, click Users.Select a user to grant permissions.Next to Command Roles, click .a. Select Org Admin. b. Click Apply Changes.

**Revoke permissions**

In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin .Under Admin > Users & Permissions, click Users.Select a user whose permissions you want to revoke.Next to Command Roles, click .a. Select None. b. Click Apply Changes.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#faq)

FAQ


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Why has my organization disappeared?[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#why-has-my-organization-disappeared)

A user must be a member at the organization level to see the organization in the dropdown when they log in. If a user is a member of an organization, they appear on the user list that Organization Admins and Site Admins can access in Command.

If your organization disappeared, it can be due to one of these reasons:

*   Your user account was removed from the organization.
    
*   The organization was deleted.
    

**Troubleshoot**

*   If you are the affected user, contact the Organization Admin and request to re-add you to the organization.
    
*   If a user has reported this to you, verify they are a member of the organization.
    

Why are cameras missing from my organization?[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#why-are-cameras-missing-from-my-organization)

Sites do not inherit users from the organization or other sites. Users who are members of the organization cannot see cameras unless they have explicitly been granted permissions to the site or sub-site where the cameras reside.

*   If you are the affected user, contact the Organization Admin or Site Admin and request access to the desired sites and subsites.
    
*   If a user has reported this to you, grant them access to the desired sites and subsites.
    

Why can’t I access certain features or settings, such as other users?[](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command#why-cant-i-access-certain-features-or-settings-such-as-other-users)

If you are unable to access certain features or settings, you don’t have sufficient permissions. Only Admins can access all features and settings.

Organization Admins are not automatically escalated to Site Admin for any site. This is a separate feature set. Therefore, Organization Admins do not inherently have permission to view any one particular site, but they can assign themselves the required roles to see their desired sites.

**Troubleshoot tips:**

*   If you are the affected user, contact the Organization Admin or Site Admin and request that they elevate your permissions to Organization Admin or the desired site or subsite.
    
*   If a user has reported this to you, elevate their permissions on the organization or desired site or subsite.
    

**Prefer to see it in action?** Check out the [video tutorial](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7ldbcKo8u0Q)
.

Last updated 1 day ago

Was this helpful?

# Third-Party VMS Integrations for Air Quality Sensor Events | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Air Quality sensors offer your organization a way to monitor essential indoor air quality factors, such as [vape index](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
, [temperature](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
, [humidity](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
, and more.

Third-party video management system (VMS) integrations allow Verkada sensors to send alert events to on-premise VMS, such as Milestone X-Protect, Wisenet WAVE, or exacqVision. These integrations allow you to receive and view sensor event data within your VMS system, eliminating the need to build custom APIs or manually match sensor events to camera footage.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-fe0498641943c044c411b519e87337b33500b76a%252F8ec4da5f1f1f0425f7a1241d4d724098c86537cb.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=463990ca&sv=2)

Each VMS integration varies based on integration prerequisites set by the manufacturer. You will receive an alert that can be easily linked to a camera and includes the sensor name, sensor reading, reading value, threshold surpassed, and timestamp.

At this time, the **video integration feature only sends alert event data**. It does not send time-series data or graph data.

#### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#supported-third-party-vms-providers)

Supported third-party VMS providers

*   Milestone X-Protect
    
*   Wisenet WAVE
    
*   exacqVision
    

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#enable-third-party-vms-integrations)

Enable third-party VMS integrations


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You need [Org Admin permissions and Site Admin permissions](https://help.verkada.com/command/users-and-permissions/roles-and-permissions-for-command)
 for each site that the sensors are located in to enable this feature.

To activate the Third-Party VMS Integration functionality on your sensors, you first need to enable the feature for your organization.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Admin .**

2

**Select Privacy & Security> Feature Manager.**

3

**Under Air Quality > Third-Party VMS Integration, select Enable from the dropdown.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#set-up-a-third-party-vms-integration)

Set up a third-party VMS integration

A sensor may only be connected to a single VMS server. Once integrated, the device will appear as **Unavailable** if a different video integration is initiated.

Sensor **must be on the same local network and VLAN** as the third-party VMS server.

1

**In Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**On the left navigation, click VMS Integration .**

3

**Select a Video Management System.**

a. Click **Submit a suggestion** to send a suggestion to our product team. b. In the top right, click **\+ Add Integration** select another supported VMS

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a5527b163c47c8f4188df12382c78bc68eb3d3d5%252F78cdc1a1b23c77dec60d0410f23da53185a383a6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=6f8e77b8&sv=2)

4

**Each VMS integration will be slightly different\*\*,\*\* but you will need to enter the following:**

a. Server **IP Address**: The IP address of your VMS server. b. Server **Port** Number: The port on your VMS server which will be able to receive events. c. (If applicable) **Username**: A configured username that is capable of receiving alerts into the system. d. (If applicable) **Password**: Password for the configured user above.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-3e07d27e46e0b6a4e4f51acb22ea301fc37b2e4a%252Fda75ba5b863422246a2242892df463009d37aea5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fcd7cf5&sv=2)

5

**Select the sensors you would like to connect and click Integrate.**

6

**The devices will begin to receive the configuration and attempt to establish a connection to the VMS server. This may take a few minutes to complete.**

* * *

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#status-indicators-on-command)

Status indicators on Command

*   Green: Successfully connected or submitted an event.
    
*   Orange: The device may be offline or has **not yet** submitted a status to the backend.
    
*   Red: Failed to connect or failed to submit an event to the VMS server.
    

The **Refresh** button checks if any of the devices have submitted any events or attempted connections to the server. It does not force the device to connect to the server.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#mange-third-party-vms-integration)

Mange Third-Party VMS Integration


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#edit-integration)

Edit integration

1

**In Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**On the left navigation, click VMS Integration .**

3

**You will see a list of existing integrations**

4

**Next to the integration you want to edit click > Edit Integration.**

a. Modify the configuration as needed. b. Click **Edit Devices.** c. Click **Save Changes.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#delete-integration)

Delete integration

1

**In Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**On the left navigation, click VMS Integration .**

3

**Next to the integration you want to delete click > Delete Intergration.**

a. Enter the confirmation code. b. Click **Delete.**

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/configuration-and-setup/third-party-vms-integrations-for-air-quality-sensor-events#what-needs-to-be-done-on-the-vms-server-side)

What needs to be done on the VMS Server Side?


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The process differs between each VMS. Refer to their documentation for precise instructions.

In general, the following steps must be completed:

*   Create generic or user defined events for each device & reading.
    
*   Create alarms for the events.
    
*   Create rules to set up custom actions such as trigger camera recording or notifications.
    
*   Create mappings between these different elements:
    
    *   Event → Alarms → Rules → 3rd Party Camera Association
        
    

You may need to repeat these steps for each device.

# Air Quality Sensor Zones | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Verkada [sensor zones](https://www.verkada.com/blog/adding-more-control-to-environmental-monitoring-with-audio-alert-and-device/)
 allow you to treat a collection of sensors as a single group or a virtual sensor. Sensor zones are designed to ensure that a single trigger source (for example, a student vaping) does not create duplicate alerts across multiple devices within the same area.

Alerts from zones are similar to alerts from individual sensors, except they also include the zone name in the alert, followed by the name of the first sensor to trigger the alert.

To use a zone effectively, you should have at least 2 devices selected. If you’re looking to set up alerts on a per-device level, we recommend using the [device-level alerts](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/configure-air-quality-event-alerts)
 instead of zone functionality.

An ongoing alert prevents the dispatch of additional alerts from any other devices in the zone for that specific sensor reading until the zone event has been resolved for at least 10 minutes.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#before-you-begin)

Before you begin


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

We recommend reviewing these guidelines before you create a sensor zone:

*   All sensors in the zone must be in the same site or the same subsite.
    
*   You can have as many zones per site as you want, with any number of sensors.
    
*   Zones are treated differently than subsites.
    
*   Sensors do not have to be at the same physical location; however, a sensor can only be a part of one zone. We recommend that sensors in a zone be in the same room or space.
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#sensor-zones)

Sensor zones


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#create-a-zone)

Create a zone

Once you create a zone you will see the sensors appear in a box with the zone label at the top left. Sensors not in a zone appear as normal.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**On the right, click Sensor Zone (above any site or subsite) to start your configuration.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-abfc892757350bd2a4ba468ab95c8a58db636693%252Fd31b7906e46327e3588097923d0897157f6dd865.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b536afdd&sv=2)

3

**On Create Sensors Zone:**

a. Give the zone a unique **Name**. b. Add devices from your site into that zone. You can only group devices from the same site into a zone. c. Click **Apply** to create the zone.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#edit-a-zone)

Edit a zone

You can still configure sensor event triggers at the device level. If you change a sensor trigger on the device level it will override what was configured for the zone. When you go to edit the zone, you will see **Mixed** for that trigger value.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Find a zone under the Summary section.**

3

**At the top right of the zone click Edit to edit the following options:**

a. Zone name. b. Selected sensors. c. Notifications. d. Delete the zone.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#mute-sensor-zone)

Mute sensor zone

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Find a zone under the Summary section.**

3

**At the top right of the zone click Edit.**

4

**Scroll down to Notifications and click next to the alert you want to mute.**

5

**Click Mute Alert:**

a. Choose the duration for the alert to mute: **1 day, 1 week, Always, or Custom.** b. If you choose **Custom**, set the duration, and click **Mute**.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#delete-sensor-zone)

Delete sensor zone

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Find a zone under the Summary section.**

3

**At the top right of the zone click Edit.**

4

**Scroll down to Notifications and click next to the alert you want to delete.**

5

**Click Delete Alert then Yes to confirm.**

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#sensor-zone-alerts)

Sensor zone alerts


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#create-zone-alerts)

Create zone alerts

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Find a zone under the Summary section.**

3

**At the top right of the zone click Edit.**

4

**Scroll down to Notifications and click Create Alert.**

5

**Continue with configuration on the Create Alert modal. See** [**Sensor Alerts and Events > Create Alert**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/configure-air-quality-event-alerts)
**.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/air-quality-sensor-zones#view-zone-alerts)

View zone alerts

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

**You are automatically redirected to the Alerts page with alerts filtered to your selected zone.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-62c5f4850042eeee5b7deb5333b36f7a090f4f5f%252F81e161107dbb1bd247d82c8437646103f14d0b05.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b1add26e&sv=2)

# Detect and Understand Carbon Monoxide | Air Quality | Verkada Help

⚠️ If your live reading is currently over 200 ppm, **contact emergency services immediately**.

**The SV25 Is not a life safety device**, and does not satisfy the requirements to be used as an emergency carbon monoxide detector.

**Do not rely solely on Verkada alerts.** These alerts do not provide a sufficient timely warning and the threat to health and safety carbon monoxide (CO) may be compromised.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#common-facts-about-carbon-monoxide)

Common facts about carbon monoxide


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#what-is-it)

What is it?

An odorless, colorless, and toxic gas. Example sources: Automobile exhaust, gas stoves, leaking chimneys, water heaters, and furnaces. Measurement range: 0—1,000 ppm

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#effects)

Effects

CO inhibits your blood from carrying oxygen even after getting to fresh air.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#exposure)

Exposure

CO is primarily a health risk when brief peak exposure is routine or levels in a space continue to rise or do not dissipate.

*   Because it’s impossible to see, taste, or smell toxic fumes, CO can be deadly and the presence in a building can be unknown.
    
*   Detection of singular large spikes do not always indicate a persistent problem or danger.
    
*   The effects of CO exposure can vary greatly from person to person depending on age, overall health, and the concentration and length of exposure.
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#understand-an-event)

Understand an event


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#example-1)

Example 1

**Scenario**: A diesel truck idling near an open window may look like this:

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8bbc4c8740121aeebe12c0b95001cca90dcca1c1%252F14ce29b68888db8ddd5aa008c362a2cb85a69dfd.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b803f3a&sv=2)

This would equate to about 35 ppm over 5 minutes. If no other events occur, the occupants of that room would have been exposed to:

*   2.917 ppm/hour
    
*   0.365 ppm/8 hours
    

In this case, the occupants might have been exposed to a peak event, but the total exposure concentration is still very low and of no need for concern. A typical meter will enter an alarm state when exposed to 15–50 ppm over an hour or a sum of 50 ppm over 8 hours.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#example-2)

Example 2

With the same example, assume that this diesel truck will make 20 stops a day. At this same spot, that would be:

*   7.2925 ppm/hour
    
*   58.34 ppm/8 hours
    

This level indicates actionable concerns, such as making an idle engine policy or closing the window. However, this would not necessarily be an emergency as there is no threat to well-being. If you begin to see events like this regularly and you cannot identify the source, you may want investigate more.

⚠️ If your fire alarm system enters an alarm state due to the presence of CO, always treat it like an emergency, even if the SV25 does not detect it.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/detect-and-understand-carbon-monoxide#example-3)

Example 3

This graph is also over the same interval of time; however, the circumstances were life-threatening conditions. Lucky for the occupants, the SV25 was mounted directly next to a certified, life safety carbon monoxide meter. **The SV25 is not a certified life-safety carbon monoxide meter.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-f65faa4e0a21ed155ad6f9dc99ab3c347a0ffca7%252Fdb149645a080bc561d63f7fe2b818121e0d72fe9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=c33e0427&sv=2)

Just like the first circumstance, the values began with a spike, however ,the level persisted to rise. The building’s fire alarm went off and the occupants were evacuated. This represents a life-threatening event. If the occupants had not evacuated, they would have been exposed to **400–500 ppm/hour**.

In this case, the SV25 was able to provide insights to the fire department to identify a failed water heater.

⚠️ If the SV25 sensor’s live reading shows unsafe values of carbon monoxide that are increasing or are not dissipating, evacuate the area immediately and contact emergency services.

Last updated 19 hours ago

Was this helpful?

# Air Quality Sensor Power Requirements | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Verkada [Environmental Sensors](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/sensors-quick-start-guide.pdf)
 use industry-standard 802.3af (Power over Ethernet \[PoE\]). The average bandwidth consumption is less than 5 kbps. Verkada [Air Quality Sensors](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 may consume additional power when performing operations, such as firmware upgrades or initial calibration.

The table reflects the maximum power draw for a particular sensor model within the normal temperature.

We recommended to provide an additional power budget on your switch for the sum of all of your sensors.

**Model**

**Normal Operation (802.3af)**

[SV11](https://www.verkada.com/sensors/sv11/)

4W

[SV21](http://sv21/)

3W

[SV23](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)

3W

[SV25](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)

3W

Last updated 17 hours ago
