# View Air Quality Sensor Data | Air Quality | Verkada Help

Verkada [Air Quality Sensors](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
 have varied readings that allow you to gain more insight into your building or monitor areas where video monitoring is not allowed.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#sensor-data-by-model)

Sensor data by model


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The data available depends on your sensor model. See [Sensor Readings](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
 for more information about the breakdown of the different sensor readings per model.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#sv21)

[SV21](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)

Sensor Reading

Data Output

**Temperature**

Room temperature

**Humidity**

Room humidity

**Heat Index**

A combined index that represents what the temperature feels like to the human body when relative humidity is combined with the temperature

**Humidex**

Humidex measures how hot we feel in hot, humid weather.

**Mold Risk Index**

The Mold Risk Index assesses the likelihood of mold growth in confined, unventilated spaces, based on temperature and humidity levels.

**Dew Point**

The dew point is the temperature to which air must be cooled, at constant pressure, for the air to reach 100% relative humidity, meaning the air becomes saturated with water vapor.

**Carbon Dioxide**

Concentration of CO2 gas, measured in ppm

**Tamper**

Indicates if the sensor is being tampered with

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#sv23)

[SV23](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)

Includes all data output of the [SV21](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
, plus the following.

Sensor Reading

Data Output

**Vape Index**

A combined index that represents the likelihood that someone is vaping in the vicinity of the sensor

**Noise Level**

Noise level in the room, measured in dB

**Air Quality Index**

U.S. Air Quality Index, derived from multiple sensors

**TVOC**

Volatile organic compound level in the air measured in an index

**PM 2.5**

**PM 4.0** **PM 10.0**

Fine particulate level measured in microgrammes per cubic meter

**Motion**

Motion detected by the Passive Infrared (PIR) sensor

**RESET® Viral Index**

The RESET® Viral Index is an index designed to assess the likelihood of airborne virus transmission in indoor spaces.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#sv25)

[SV25](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)

Includes all data output of the [SV23](https://docs.verkada.com/docs/air-quality-sensors-overview.pdf)
, plus the following.

Sensor Reading

Data Output

**Carbon Monoxide**

Concentration of Carbon Monoxide gas, measured in ppm

**Formaldehyde (CH2O)**

Concentration of Formaldehyde (CH2O) gas, measured in ppb

**Barometric Pressure**

Measurement of air pressure in the atmosphere

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#sv11)

[SV11](https://www.verkada.com/sensors/sv11/)

Verkada’s first-generation sensor outputs data on the following readings.

Sensor Reading

Data Output

**Vape Index**

A combined index that represents the likelihood that someone is vaping in the vicinity of the sensor

**Temperature**

Room temperature

**Humidity**

Room humidity

**Heat Index**

A combined index that represents what the temperature feels like to the human body when relative humidity is combined with the temperature

**Humidex**

Humidex measures how hot we feel in hot, humid weather.

**Mold Risk Index**

The Mold Risk Index assesses the likelihood of mold growth in confined, unventilated spaces, based on temperature and humidity levels.

**Dew Point**

The dew point is the temperature to which air must be cooled, at constant pressure, for the air to reach 100% relative humidity, meaning the air becomes saturated with water vapor.

**Noise Level**

Noise level in the room, measured in dB

**Air Quality Index**

U.S. Air Quality Index, derived from multiple sensors

**TVOC**

Volatile organic compound level in the air, measured in parts per million

**PM 2.5**

**PM 4.0** **PM 10.0**

Fine particulate level measured in micrograms per cubic meter

**Tamper**

Indicates if the sensor is being tampered with

**Motion**

Motion detected by the PIR sensor

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#view-details-about-your-sensor)

View details about your sensor


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Click a sensor device to go to the sensor’s Details page.**

3

**Select the sensor reading you want to see. Then select the time range for which you would like to view. By default, you should see the output of Today for the selected reading.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4033bb26fa1ecaed455f61e83e36bc715b4fcd8e%252Fff989ea7e66a672094e4684f47eb2ba324e3bae7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2339c828&sv=2)

4

**Select which reading you want to view. For a detailed view, select from the list. Learn more about** [**sensor readings**](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/air-quality-sensor-readings)
**.**

As you scrub through the graph, the side readings also follow the time frame you hover over.

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-032d05dd20c15e103c2340c5094fa0489ee0e796%252F580c397ba66bd34a9fc284b3353b2733dec0953d.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=77b483bc&sv=2)

When you select a reading from the list on the left, the **Alerts** section below filters alerts for the selected reading. You can view all alerts by changing the filter on the right to **All Sensors**.

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#select-a-time-range-and-custom-date-range)

Select a time range and custom date range


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Select a sensor to customize the time range.**

3

**Above the graph, select the dropdown menu and choose the date range of preset options (This Hour, This Week, This Month, This Year) to understand your device’s environment over a range of time. To return to the live sensor readings, at the top of the list, select Live.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0ffe28ad7eff0a2d7e76a2655767abe6812a0f9b%252Fe169867e9a71378b19580a82b5f6a6449e87955a.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=86ebeaea&sv=2)

4

**(Optional) Specify a custom or present range using one of these options:**

*   On the dropdown menu above the graph, select **Custom** to specify a range of time from the calendar, and click **Apply**. (As your date range increases, the resolution of your chart decreases.)
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-87595f2419c8b2ffecf30255c7aa47a4bfe4bffe%252Faf0166e2ee88bee6d1ddaf49f3748a4eb1372d42.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a6928133&sv=2)
    
*   Click and drag the cursor over the desired time frame. This zooms in on the data. (Click **Reset** to zoom out to the original time frame.) This can be useful in understanding how long-term and macro changes in your environment, such as seasons, can affect air quality or cleaning habits.
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#data-retention-and-resolution)

Data retention and resolution


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Verkada sensors store sensor data for 365 days. After the 365th day, the oldest sensor data is overwritten with the newest data.

*   For the SV11, data is stored at a **1-second** resolution for **30 days**. For **days 31–365**, data is stored at a **5-minute** resolution.
    
*   For the SV20 series, data is stored at a **5-second** resolution for **30 days**. For days **31–365**, data is stored at a **5-minute** resolution.
    

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/sensor-data/view-air-quality-sensor-data#export-sensor-data-and-alerts)

Export sensor data and alerts

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Air Quality.**

2

**Select a sensor.**

3

**On the toolbar, click the Download as CSV icon to export sensor data or sensor alert data via a comma-separated value (CSV) file.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6a2463010b5f4a409c4210735fdddf07d72383c7%252Fa9f92bacc6f19fa3346c4ad5f6137401f6082761.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=30881289&sv=2)

4

**On Download CSV**

a. Select **Sensor Data** or **Alerts**, depending on what type of data you want to download. b. Check the box next to the sensor readings you want to download. By default, the temperature is Fahrenheit. You can choose Celsius, if preferred. c. Set the date range (**Last 5 Minutes**, **Last Hour**, **Last Day**, **Last Week**, **Last Month**, **Last Year**, **Custom**) for the report. d. Choose the resolution (**1 Minute**, **5 Minutes**, **30 Minutes**, **1 Hour**, **1 Day**) and then click **Export**. ​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057705728-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJtgmyWYlTEX9DpjvBwTL%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c27ddcad9cbf94654665e3823b205d403fa98326%252F62554bfee349f2b293a95f93f72cc9ddcd033569.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=45ce76b1&sv=2)

For sensor data, you can export data at various predefined resolutions (5s, 1min, 5min, 30min, 1hr, 1day). The table shows the maximum resolution that can be exported for a given time range.

**Time Range**

**Maximum Resolution**

1 hour

5 seconds

1–24 hours

1 minute

24 hours–30 days

5 minutes

30–180 days

30 minutes

180–365 days

1 hour

Once you click **Export**, Command sends an email with the CSV attached. This process can take up to 10 minutes, depending on the amount of data being requested.

# Set Up the BC82 Alarm Console | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

The Verkada BC82 alarm console is used to arm/disarm alarm sites, with additional functionality, including a digital panic button, device status page, event feed, integrated camera, microphone for remote monitoring and talk-down from Verkada Command, 90db siren, and a built-in wireless hub to connect wireless sensors.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0372668182addf3419cd52b426b155e3edc10352%252Fc3519f48467a6b01020bf991acb770567750beb8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=babe8378&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#before-you-begin)

**Before you begin**


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before you begin the setup, review the requirements and recommendations.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#requirements)

Requirements

The BC82 requires 802.3at for power and network connectivity and includes a mounting bracket and the associated mounting hardware.

**Note**: The alarm console must be mounted in portrait mode/vertically.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#recommendation)

Recommendation

Once you take the alarm console out of the box, we recommend that you stage the console and test its functionality before mounting:

1

**Attach an Ethernet cable to the BC82 located on the back of the console.**

2

**Connect the Ethernet cable to an open port on a Power over Ethernet (PoE) (802.3at) switch.**

**Note:** When you first plug in the BC82, it may take a few minutes to build enough charge to boot. After a few minutes of the device being plugged in, press the power button located on the back to turn the console on.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-e27f1f6de9450fe7f3825da5c9b1f78d2f150aa2%252Fb9f5c39400bd000f537ec43ce27468dbad233b08.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=e5291d76&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#add-the-device-to-command)

Add the device to Command


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**Once the console powers on, using the serial number located on the box or on the console display, add the device to Command via the web interface.**

2

**In Command, ensure the console is added to the appropriate alarm site.**

3

**If the console has network connectivity to Verkada servers and the serial number has been added to Command, you should be redirected to this keypad interface:**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c9efe960e45ad5500b7c13d49482c048ec2ca93a%252Fcc986a939aa7e4fdb3f715998fc101f2f8b0ab3c.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5698ec7f&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#test-keypad-features)

Test keypad features


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Prior to mounting to its final location, test the keypad features to ensure everything is working as expected:

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#home-screen)

Home screen

The home screen shows status events of critical issues (yellow box) and sensors with activity (blue box). You can touch either box to pull up the associated devices.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#camera-page)

Camera page

From the home screen, swipe left to see the camera view. From here, you can select cameras in the site and view them.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-9d0f5c3d10d2e7d183609426bc33c228ed69865f%252F580443c76f044a7ea5aa40be6c382569d6e76d73.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=2aa9c109&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#devices-page)

Devices page

From the home screen, swipe right to go to the devices page. From here, you can see all devices and the last event that exists in the alarm site. This should mirror the **Devices** tab in the Alarms site in Command. ​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-98bd09aa6553431dbb93b47be8fd65df7885796d%252Fca243c612d6fae8843d5cfb715c3c499062dccbc.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fe9085eb&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#arm-tab)

Arm tab

On the **Arm** tab, you can test arm/disarm functionality with your [configured key codes](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings)
 in Command.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#two-way-talk-down-and-listening-in)

Two-Way Talk-Down and Listening In

**Recommendation**. This test is best performed with two people in separate rooms. Please have one individual in front of the console and the other on the Command web interface.

On the Command UI, the Alarm console should display a live feed.

*   To test the listen-in feature, unmute the alarm console, where you should hear the sounds that the console is picking up.
    
*   To test two-way talk-down, initiate a video call by pressing the **Call** button in the video feed of the console.
    

**Note**: From Command, the Alarm console includes an integrated camera and microphone for remote monitoring. A banner at the top of the Alarm console screen indicates when video or audio is being viewed or recorded.

You can also choose to plug in a 3.5-mm audio jack to the console for broader/louder coverage for talk-down communications, including outdoor speakers.

**Note:** To use the 3.5-mm audio jack, you need to use a speaker amp to increase the volume from the console.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#panic-button)

Panic button

Press the digital panic button to test an immediate alarm. You can disarm it with your configured key codes or via the Command web interface.

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-the-bc82-alarm-console#add-wireless-sensors)

Add wireless sensors


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You have two options on how to add new wireless sensors:

*   Via the main devices page and enter the serial number
    
*   On the Alarms devices page, click the plus (**+**) symbol > **Add wireless sensors**.
    

Once events occur or on the first boot of the sensor, you should see the connection from the BC82 to the sensor.

**Note:** If there are multiple hubs in the area (for example, BC82 or BH61), the sensors will join to the closest hub device (hub with the best signal strength).

After testing these features, you can proceed to mount the alarm console in its final location using the mounting instructions included in the box.

Last updated 23 hours ago

Was this helpful?

# Set Up and Install Wireless Sensors | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

Building materials, obstructions, distance, and general radio frequency (RF) interference are highly variable across different environments and from time of day. As a result, we highly suggest you adhere to the following guidelines to ensure that your wireless system operates to the best of its ability.

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/set-up-and-install-wireless-sensors#add-your-wireless-hub-to-verkada-command)

Add your wireless hub to Verkada Command


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**Remove the cover from your alarm hub and plug the device into a Power over Ethernet (PoE) switch.**

2

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Device. Alternatively, you can go to All Products > Add Devices (and skip step 3).**

3

**Select your wireless hub.**

4

**At the top, click Add Devices. Enter the 12-character serial number located on the sensor or on the box that was provided. Alternatively, you can scan the QR code.**

5

**Once you add your wireless hub, it is assigned to the Unassigned Devices site. Follow the setup flow to configure your device name, site, and location.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-5ee2c9062ec096db846b01bafe759090944cef7b%252Fde969f1ac67b95a95ea4b875fb9397e9c69d64f9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=af1adc1f&sv=2)

6

**Go to the Alarms Devices tab and verify that your wireless hub is reporting online and the LED on the hub is solid blue.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-04ce43dbedaa9232ce2bbc33e66c891fdc1fb003%252F9d5df4044057f4e49e38913cbfffac45a81c4855.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=fd194c5f&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/set-up-and-install-wireless-sensors#add-your-wireless-sensors-to-verkada-command)

Add your wireless sensors to Verkada Command


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Place your wireless sensors right next to the wireless hub. At Verkada, we verify that all of your sensors are properly communicating with your hub and reporting events to Command before installing the sensors in their final locations.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Device > Add Devices. Alternatively, you can go to All Products > Add Devices.**

2

**Enter the 12-character serial number located on the sensor or on the box that was provided and select Add Device.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-51ad16b55259110e056452fdf1197d6b95fb98e7%252F158a15242e886891b3a147bce7c78cc097e7895b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b5f42f08&sv=2)

3

**Once you add your wireless hub, it is assigned to the Unassigned Devices site. Follow the setup flow to configure your device name, site, and location.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-84236f817dc6958938b8fb9b4ceb852988424599%252F59a443dc74b6b13798d98e7df9cd063587459b46.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=878a8d4d&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/set-up-and-install-wireless-sensors#power-on-your-wireless-sensors)

Power on your wireless sensors


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When the sensors are first powered on, they automatically try to join the closest hub.

1

**Pull the battery tabs from your sensor(s) to power on the device. The sensors should automatically connect to the closest hub and appear online in Command. If not, show that they are connected to a hub; perform these steps:**

a. Power cycle the sensor by completely removing the batteries and re-adding the batteries to the sensor. b. Initiate trigger event(s) as detailed in the [Wireless Deep Dive](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-your-wireless-alarm-devices)
 guide above for your particular sensor (door open/close, motion detected, button press, tamper, and so on.)

2

**Once the sensor(s) have communicated with a hub, the sensors show under their respective hub that they are connected to. From there, you can get/set the following information:**

*   Set the name of the sensor
    
*   Display the sensor type
    
*   Display the last event
    
*   Sensor serial number
    
*   Battery level
    
*   Signal strength
    
*   Attaching nearby camera(s) to the sensor
    
*   Configure the sensor ​
    

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6540d883b7c323142926e1b889dcde88d7fed6c8%252F38efcc6e80046d2222efdf155405de8b1b850732.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=edff80a6&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/set-up-and-install-wireless-sensors#validate-wireless-sensor-coverage)

Validate wireless sensor coverage


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You should place the hub as close to the desired location as possible, such as the center of the floor/building for maximum coverage.

*   The most recent sensor events are time-stamped in the Alarms site > **Devices** tab. You can monitor this page to ensure that sensor events are being reported to Command and the sensor’s current signal strength.
    
*   Relocate your wireless sensors to their desired install locations and send several trigger events (door open/close, motion detected, panic button press, glass break tester, and shorting the metal contacts on the water sensor).
    
*   Received Signal Strength Indicator (RSSI) values should be greater than –80 (for example, –75, –70, and so on) to account for variability in each environment as well as ensure there are no offline events for your devices once fully installed. When signal strength is confirmed, you can install the sensor in its final location and send one more event for good measure, otherwise:
    
    *   If no events are being received, move closer to the hub to determine if the issue is related to signal coverage.
        
    *   If you find that events are being received when you move closer to the hub, perform a site walk to determine if any obstructions could be dampening the signal. (walls, metal frames, windows, and so on).
        
    *   You can also choose to reposition the hub for better coverage and restart the testing.
        
    *   If the above fails, you may want to consider purchasing an additional hub to fully cover your floor/building.
        
    

Last updated 23 hours ago

# Configure Camera Alarm Trigger Events | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

Verkada’s camera alarm triggers provide additional information to the monitoring agent to determine if the event is a threat to a person or property. You can also get [alerts](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts)
 based on the alarm triggers configured.

Vehicle detection events are **not video-verified** and will automatically raise an alarm.

For more information on the types of alarm triggers see below:

*   [Person detection](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#h_0f8f2047f8)
    
*   [Line crossing](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#h_71ccaf8225)
    
*   [Loitering](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#h_f4fc8818d9)
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#when-should-a-detection-occur)

When should a detection occur?


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a Verkada camera detects an object, green bounding boxes appear over the detected object(s). You can see these bounding boxes when scrubbing through a camera’s [people and vehicle motion search](https://help.verkada.com/verkada-cameras/analytics-and-detection/people-and-vehicle-motion-search)
 or scrubbing through a camera’s historical video.

Detection is determined when the center bottom of a person’s bounding box crosses a line or sits inside a loitering region (in the majority of cases, it is a person’s feet).

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4af1dc445f323aa34ddcfc90e253e3f8489c610d%252Ff67bf5a923d65ebec1716839c6cbda6a2a32cda9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=94a5ef66&sv=2)

Trigger Point

Trigger Point

Use line crossing and loitering detection instead of person detection when available. Loitering detection and line crossing are only available on the CF81 and third-generation or newer cameras (models that end in "2" or higher), except the CP52.

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#configure-alarm-triggers)

Configure alarm triggers


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Alarms.**

2

**Select a site, at the top left, click Settings.**

3

**Under Settings, go to Alarm Triggers.**

4

**On Camera Events:**

a. Click **Select Cameras.** b. Select a camera to configure. c. Configure the trigger type(s) as needed. d. Click **Done.**

5

**A trigger badge appears on the camera to indicate which trigger type has been enabled.**

6

**(Optional) Repeat step 4 on other cameras as needed.**

7

**Click Done when finished.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-12778901c56cb48a7c099e89d83efe4a2099c6d5%252Fbdd9ba55dcedf8371e29e9946c048b5eca356ffd.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=186652e3&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#alarm-triggers)

Alarm triggers


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#person-detection)

Person detection

Person detection is determined whenever any part of a person’s bounding box intersects with the configured region of interest. ​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0229492c11b75e418fe1b9fd7a605b6109d0f9a0%252F8a96c77c20687c749674a427e63ea46eaa0e9e87.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=a1a9992a&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#line-crossing-recommended)

Line Crossing (recommended)

Line crossing provides more control and granularity in a trigger by allowing you to define a unidirectional or bidirectional line that a person has to cross before detection occurs.

You can define a maximum of 4 lines and choose the direction you expect people or vehicles to cross. ​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-ecb2cdf1e8d4b164d80d58630bbbe35d72d391d4%252F336562a42cbe236201a6fd038881003f353163c0.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cef57f92&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#loitering-detection)

Loitering detection

Loitering detection allows you to define a region with a freeform polygon and define how long a person has to stay in that region before detection occurs.

Define up to 4 freeform polygon regions and define how long a person has to stay in that region before detection occurs.

#### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-camera-alarm-trigger-events#how-it-works)

How it works

1

**Once the person’s trigger point intersects the loitering region, the timer begins.**

2

**If the trigger point remains in this region for the configured time (one minute default) a detection event occurs.**

3

**If the person’s trigger point briefly exits and re-enters the loitering region within 4 seconds, the counter continues.**

4

**If the camera loses track of an individual (for example, walking out of frame) or the trigger point is outside the loitering region for more than 4 seconds, the counter resets.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-63ff6d488d8cf0fcaa8968405b80b25792ed4e8c%252F7897160efa8b9ec66bf5e3659cb0d73f13f3c6ca.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1009a4b9&sv=2)

Last updated 1 day ago

Was this helpful?

# Configure Alarms Event Alerts | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

You can enable alerts for a variety of Alarms events, depending on your configuration needs. For more information about the Alarms event types see [below](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_1cfb1d78c7)
.

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#configure-alarms-event-alerts)

Configure Alarms event alerts


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#create-alert-greater-than-events)

Create Alert > Events

1

**Log in to Verkada Command.**

2

**On the Command homepage, left navigation, click Alerts .**

3

**On the Alerts page, next to My Alerts, click .**

4

**On Select Event, select the Alarms product type.**

5

**Search for or select an event to configure.**

6

**(Optional) Some event types are general and have more specific options once you select them. If prompted, complete any additional configuration steps then click Next.**

7

**Select your devices/sites, based on the alert type you can configure events to be device-specific, site-specific, or all devices.**

*   When you select **Sites** or **All Devices**, new devices added after alert creation will automatically generate alerts.
    

Click **Done** to continue.

8

**(Optional) Some event types have additional setup steps. If that is the case, click the additional steps and follow the prompts in the configuration window.**

9

**Click Done and continue with the alert** [**recipients**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_0b37105bb2)
**.**

**Note**: Wired sensors are not currently supported as individual selectable devices, but you can select **Sites** or **All Devices** to configure alerts for them.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#create-alert-greater-than-recipients)

Create Alert > Recipients

1

**On Recipients, you can search for or select other Command users individually or you can assign the alert to a group.**

2

**Select the dropdown menu next to a user or group to choose their notification method(s). Recipients can be notified either via a push notification, SMS, or email.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-a30e5c666efe865b169b36f277c2ab798ad76c5d%252F3a9609d9912905edd0f35abfff403a95e0b820c8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4d04bdcf&sv=2)

3

**(Optional) By default, you will be added to the alert created. To remove yourself, select the dropdown menu and click Delete.**

4

**Click Done and continue with the alert** [**notification schedule**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_1133acf090)
**.**

**Note:** Any recipient added to this alert will see it appear under the **Shared Alerts** section of their **Alerts** page.

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#create-alert-greater-than-notification-schedule)

Create Alert > Notification Schedule

1

**On Notification Schedule, you must specify what days and times you want alerts to be sent. By default, events are generated 24/7.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-b9042c786a9dd12580abefdd20f412fe59cbac5e%252F7b61969c185d482c85ec3b7f15a687d75aee8d13.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5dbfda6f&sv=2)

2

**Click Done and continue with the alert** [**device actions**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_1e427ac1c0)
 **or** [**finish the alert**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_06c9e92cba)
**.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#create-alert-greater-than-device-action)

Create Alert > Device Action

In addition to notifying individuals, you can configure your horn speaker to play when an alert is triggered. These alerts can be text-to-speech or an uploaded MP3 file.

1

**On Device Action, select the horn speaker(s) you want to play your message.**

2

**Select your device’s notification preference (Text to Speech or Audio File).**

a. For **Text to Speech,** enter the desired message up to 200 characters. b. For **Audio File,** drag and drop the file or click **choose a file** to upload your audio clip.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-6eebd070cac52d81c895573628cb7b21ba245804%252Fbd7aa4597a411933461874e312ac1e72683f4dab.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1296423c&sv=2)

3

**Click Done and continue with** [**finish the alert**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#h_06c9e92cba)
**.**

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#finish-the-alert)

Finish the alert

1

**Click Next on the bottom right of the configuration window once you have configured all the desired alert settings.**

2

**Enter a descriptive name for the alert.**

3

**Click Done and you will start to receive alerts.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-75fcc30636d14fdd34cc9e376db710c1542f4ef2%252F943420792c6bfe40aee47eab735038e52669e4ac.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=cab60c29&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/events-and-alerts/configure-alarms-event-alerts#understand-the-various-alarms-event-types)

Understand the various Alarms event types

**Alert Type**

**Description**

**Online/Offline**

Alarms device changed state to online or offline.

**Alarm Site Status**

Alarm site changed state to armed or disarmed.

**Cellular Module Status**

Selected cellular backup is in one or many of the following states

**Active:** currently in use

​**On Standby:** Connected to the cellular network and not in use

**Disconnected:** Cell backup was disconnected from the device

**Offline:** Unable to connect to the cellular network

**Sensor Events**

Receive an alert when one of the following events is detected:

Door Opened

Door Held Opened

Glass Break Detected

Motion Detected

Panic Button Pressed

Water Detected

**Device Power Status**

A wireless sensor battery state changed.

**Tamper**

Interference or manipulation detected on an Alarms device.

# Troubleshoot Inrush Current Issues | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/troubleshooting/troubleshoot-inrush-current-issues#before-you-begin)

Before you begin


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To help you troubleshoot inrush issues and what causes them, familiarize yourself with these terms:

*   **Capacitance**—The capability of a material to store electrical charge. Capacitors are the physical component that adds capacitance in electrical circuits.
    
*   **Inrush current**—Also called _input surge current_ or _switch-on surge_—the maximal instantaneous input current that is drawn by an electric device when it is first turned on. Generally speaking, the **higher** the capacitance of a device, the **higher** the inrush current draw that an individual device will have.
    

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/troubleshooting/troubleshoot-inrush-current-issues#understand-how-an-inrush-current-causes-problems)

Understand how an inrush current causes problems


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The image shown illustrates a large current draw when a device is first powered on that decreases into a steady-state current. The peak and the inrush current magnitude depends on the **number** and **type** of capacitors that are in an electrical circuit.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-45284fdda0392732aba44b13cbd4619b992feaac%252F6f38678e6b7200db2982f779d42be83321e7cf04.jpg%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=9f64efcb&sv=2)

What is Inrush Current?

What is Inrush Current?

The image shown below is an example of 2 different motion sensors that have different capacitance levels despite the data sheet reporting similar power requirements.

**Motion Sensor**

**Power**

**Example**

**Honeywell IS335 (2 Capacitors)**

9–15VDC @ 12mA

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c829dabf304a351c60db2ff8523c67e93e153b29%252F6bdad259cc8a7d026434c14a568b1a7153fe829b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3af71b0c&sv=2)

**Honeywell DT7235T (10+ Capacitors)**

7.5–16VDC @ 24mA

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-c78667e449e90eaee693b176bd1f2b207fb2ce3b%252Fca6ff4025bcc6376edcac3e50986c767ee3ca490.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=300&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=5de0994d&sv=2)

The Honeywell DT7235T has a **significantly higher capacitance and inrush current** compared to the Honeywell IS335 due to the number and size of capacitors needed to support its DUAL TEC functionality.

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/troubleshooting/troubleshoot-inrush-current-issues#how-to-identify-capacitance-issues)

How to identify capacitance issues


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Generally speaking, capacitance issues present in 1 of 2 ways, as shown in the example of the [BP41 Alarm Panel](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/configure-and-wire-inputsoutputs-on-the-bp41)
.

*   **Immediately after wiring in a high capacitance device**. The inrush current of the device is so high that it causes a **brownout** where the panels **lose power** due to an internal protective mechanism to protect the system from a short.
    
*   **After a power cycle, reboot, or firmware upgrade on the BP41**. The combined power requirements of system boot and inrush current of **all devices** **at once** exceed what can be supplied by the panel, again, causing a brownout where the panel loses power. This issue is not seen during the initial install because:
    
    *   The panel is already in a fully booted state.
        
    *   External sensors are added and wired in one-by-one, and each individual component is given enough time to charge its capacitors.
        
    
*   **There is an "AUX Output Failure" warning on the device and "AUX power disabled" warning shown in the alarm site.** The AUX is disabled to avoid the inrush issue from the 4-wire sensors and allow the system continue to boot and remain online. ​
    

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/troubleshooting/troubleshoot-inrush-current-issues#what-to-expect)

What to expect

This can cause the panel to:

*   Fail to boot up completely until the sensors are removed from power
    
    OR
    
*   Introduce delays in boot up until the capacitors on the devices are charged enough to bypass the internal protective mechanism.
    

The panel typically has its Panel Status LED (OFF) and the Power LED (ON).

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8928842c733ea1f6d5102dc7a8931f2b2a4c220d%252F52a9934b430d667c5e7a2be76a294b88c49a6e04.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=4c56c34b&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/troubleshooting/troubleshoot-inrush-current-issues#how-to-solve-problems-with-inrush-current)

How to solve problems with inrush current


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

1

**We recommend wiring a 100Ω resistor inline to the power of each of the sensors to help slow down current draw from the sensors and avoid a brownout.**

​

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-34047fe4ab9c8f3592bb588bfe9d7943b4fb0e8c%252Fbadd9f117ddde9dda8ae5d10d9f7c9b32f4b0630.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d938ffbe&sv=2)

2

**After wiring in the resistors, confirm system operation by power cycling the panel and to ensure that the panel boots up properly.**

# Configure Classic Alarms Site Settings | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

When you create a Classic Alarms site in Verkada Command, you need to go through a few steps to configure settings for the site.

You can modify these settings at any time:

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Alarms.**

2

**Select the site that you want to configure.**

3

**Configure your alarm site using the** [**Settings**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#h_7a41c203f0)
 [**options**](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#h_7a41c203f0)
 **below.**

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-settings)

Alarm settings


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Click to expand each option below to learn more about settings options.

General[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#general)

On the **General** page, specify the physical location of your Alarms site. Ensure this address is accurate and specific. Verkada uses this address in case emergency services need to be dispatched. Each unique address requires one Alarms license.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-b4f727d79325a15b736d118445e805ae04b2571f%252Fd50a1cde3e195a117b84644e3a42eb2c4aece557.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d4b30634&sv=2)

Alarm triggers[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-triggers)

You can choose which events should trigger an alarm: cameras, sensor inputs, and doors. The events that exist in this Alarms site can be selected as _alarm triggers_. This means that when the site is armed, any of the following events can trip the alarm.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0cf5b1bb50feb06f83a23adebc3a69fbc7a7328b%252Ffcdd133335b45b9644986ba4138a71d69cb44113.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=56455d21&sv=2)

**When alarm devices go offline**

By default, if any alarm devices go offline for more than five minutes while the system is in an armed state, it automatically raises the alarm and sends an offline notification to the users on the contact list.

If any alarm devices go offline while the system is in an _unarmed_ state:

*   It records the offline event and sends a notification to the users on the contact list, but does not raise an alarm.
    
*   It does not raise an alarm when the system is armed later, unless the Alarm device comes online and goes offline for more than five minutes.
    

**Change default behavior of offline events**

To change the default behavior of offline events:

Navigate to **Settings** > **Offline Events**.

Select **Raise alarm**, **Notify only**, or **Do nothing** in the event a selected device goes offline.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-7d12439b35067b9a3cdb5c37dbab38d6b5094ba3%252F927c3c4f0ff3524e42e6b62fc56bb653e8b98692.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b6a81b8e&sv=2)

Cameras[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#cameras)

To enable a camera as an alarm trigger:

On **Select Cameras**, select the camera for person detection. Once selected, anytime the system is armed and a person is detected, a video verification event is logged and sent to our monitoring agents for review.

Click **Done** when you’re done with your selection.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252F3grM98EyYW0Ea662JJOk%252Fimage%2520%284%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc856dee7-fec5-4636-b515-335c39de4907&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=949b42e4&sv=2)

**Specify a region of interest**

You can specify a region of interest where the selected region (in blue) is the only area where person detection is running; everything outside of the blue box is ignored.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252FSaRKe5zoBR9AnfRuoZq9%252Fimage%2520%283%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Daa769836-b2ef-4235-8f4b-03157d1ff0a6&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=d1aac246&sv=2)

Wired sensors[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#wired-sensors)

An alarm panel detects a relevant state change (door open, glass break, water detected, motion detected, and so on).

Wireless sensors[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#wireless-sensors)

Configure wireless sensor-specific settings:

**Door Sensor**

*   **Sensitivity Level (Low, Medium, High)**—The higher the sensitivity, the greater distance allowed between the sensor and the magnet to register a closed event.
    
*   **Universal Transmitter Mode (Normally Open, Normally Closed)**—Allows the door contact sensor to be utilized as a wireless transmitter, turning any standard 2-wire sensor into a wireless signal
    

**Panic button**

**Button Press Pattern (Single, Long, Double, Triple)**—Allows you to specify the type of button press pattern required to send a panic signal.

Access control[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#access-control)

An access controller detects a door open, door held open or door forced open event.

Alarm console[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-console)

You can configure an alarm console as a trigger by using person detection on its camera.

Air quality sensor events[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#air-quality-sensor-events)

A sensor detects motion, changes in temperature, humidity, air quality, and so on.

**Required.** [Air Quality Sensor Thresholds](https://help.verkada.com/air-quality/events-and-alerts/configure-air-quality-event-alerts)
 must be configured for the particular readings that you want to use as a trigger to raise an alarm.

Offline events[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#offline-events)

Set the desired response when an alarm device goes offline.

Alarm responses[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-responses)

Video Verification

If enabled, video verification allows for a Verkada monitoring agent to review video footage of an incident before raising an alarm. This reduces the likelihood of false alarms. You can configure these levels of security for video verification:

*   **Normal Security**—An alarm is only raised if there is a visible threat to a person or property. For example, a person brandishing a weapon, broken glass, etc.
    
*   **Max Security**—An alarm is raised if a person is present or if there are any signs of an intrusion. This alarm level helps to significantly reduce the chance of a false alarm occurring.
    
*   **Customer Security**—An administrator can choose what the monitoring agent will raise an alarm for depending on the video [verification rules](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/verification-rules)
    .
    

Organizations that create their _**first**_ Alarms site on or after\*\* June 29, 2024, \*\*will no longer be able to select a video verification security level; the Alarms site will operate under max security verification.

**Use case of trip event**

Site is armedA camera detects a janitor in a safe roomTrip event occursVideo clip of the event is sent to the monitoring agent for review

In _normal security_ mode, the agent determines that there is no visible threat to people or property and an alarm is not raised. In _max security_ mode, the agent raises an alarm immediately if a person is present when the site is armed.

For video verification to be active for non-camera devices, you need to link your devices to nearby cameras that can provide context for alarm events. For air quality sensors and doors, the cameras you’ve previously associated with those devices are automatically used for video verification.

For BH61 / BP41 sensor inputs, you can manually add nearby cameras when you configure those inputs.

For more information on the video verification rules, refer to [Verification Rules](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/verification-rules)
. ​

**Emergency Dispatch**

If emergency dispatch is enabled, the Verkada monitoring agent contacts the individuals in the order of your contact list. If an emergency is confirmed or if no one can be reached, the agent dispatches emergency services to the site address.

You must have at least one [contact](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings)
 with a valid phone number listed to use emergency dispatch.

*   **Immediate Dispatch on Panic**
    
    When enabled, Verkada monitoring agents dispatch emergency services immediately without confirming with contact list. This _only_ applies to duress and panic alarms. Notification recipients still receive a call/SMS to get visibility into the situation.
    
*   **Monitoring Test Mode** If enabled, the Verkada monitoring agent still reaches out in the order of your contact list, but does _not_ dispatch emergency services if they are unable to reach you.
    
*   **Permit Number (Optional)**
    
    You can optionally add a permit number to be shared with emergency services when dispatch is requested. _This is sometimes a requirement in certain counties and states_ and should be acquired via local Verkada Partner as requirements differ across jurisdictions. You can also provide property entry or gate codes for monitoring team to provide to emergency services:
    
    ![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-4597c5f002562060870dcdefe1497fe02950f066%252F63a83ed3019308566fd244f2de7db373ab1e1486.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=bbc0433d&sv=2)
    
*   **Emergency Dispatch Context Cameras** By default, our monitoring agents do not have any access to your cameras. This setting allows you to grant **live-only** access to a **maximum of 10 cameras** in addition to any footage that has been video verified to gather additional context during an active alarm.
    

Contact list[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#contact-list)

Configure Command users to be notified via SMS and/or email notifications when an alarm is raised. These notifications can be sent, regardless of whether emergency dispatch is enabled.

By default, all users will receive SMS and email notifications, but need to be explicitly designated as emergency dispatch contacts. To do that, click the **Dispatcher** icon. The call order is determined by the number to the right of the **Dispatcher** icon.

**Important**. Please ask users on the notification list to save the following numbers to their contact list as "Verkada Monitoring".

These are the numbers that we use to notify you of an emergency:

**SMS**

+16193298928

+16193298846

+16193298736

**Phone call**

+16193044016

Alarm actions[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-actions)

You can configure which actions to take when an alarm is raised:

*   **Alarm panel outputs**
    
    If you have a BP41 alarm panel, you can configure outputs A and B on the panel to provide 12V of power to sirens, strobes, and other alarm signaling devices in the event of an alarm. Find setup instructions [here](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/configure-and-wire-inputsoutputs-on-the-bp41)
    .
    
*   **Wireless outputs**
    
    If you have a BX21, you can configure the wireless relay as an output for a siren, strobe, or other alarm signaling devices. Find setup instructions [here](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/configure-a-bx21-wireless-relay)
    .
    
*   **Pay alert message**
    
    You can also choose to play an alert message on the alarm console.
    
*   **Access control lockdown**
    
    You can leverage a configured [lockdown](https://help.verkada.com/access-control/configuration-and-setup/emergency-lockdown)
     scenario through Verkada access control as a response to an alarm being raised.
    

* * *

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#arm-disarm-settings)

Arm/Disarm settings

Setting

Description

**Entry Delay**

Number of seconds to wait after a trigger event occurs before raising an alarm.

**Exit Delay**

Number of seconds to wait after entering the code entry before arming site.

**Geofence Arm/Disarm**

Restricts mobile app arm/disarm when the user is within 200 meters of the alarm site.

**Note:** The Verkada Alarms app will be required to arm/disarm for users with Site Viewer permissions or lower.

**Arm Schedule**

Automatically arms the site during the specified window.

**Auto Re-Arm**

If disarmed during the arm period, automatically re-arms the site after a set period of time.

**Auto Disarm**

Automatically disarms the site at the end of the schedule.

**Arm/Disarm Notification Window**

Receive a notification whenever an arm/disarm occurs within a specific time range.

**Output on Arm**

A wired output is enabled when the site is armed and disabled when it is disarmed.

**Disarm via Doors**

Select which doors automatically disarm the site when the door is unlocked via a badge swipe. This option is only available if a door exists in the site.

**Arm via Doors**

Select which doors automatically arm the site when the door is unlocked via a badge swipe. This option is only available if a door exists in the site.

**Note**: The exit delay is 20 seconds.

**Toggle via Doors**

Toggle between armed/disarmed for this site when one of these doors grant access.

**Keycodes**

You can add multiple site keycodes that arm/disarm the system and individual [user keycodes](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/generate-a-user-or-general-keycode-with-classic-alarms)
.

**Duress Keycode**

You can enter this code to trigger a panic alarm on the alarm console in case of an emergency. When a duress code is entered into the console, the system disarms the site, but still triggers alarm notifications and emergency dispatch (if enabled).

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/configuration-and-setup/configure-classic-alarms-site-settings#alarm-console-settings)

Alarm console settings

Here are the settings you can configure for the alarm console.

Setting

Description

**Enable Console Video Recording**

Gives users access to live and historical video from the alarm console in Command.

**Enable Console Video Stream**

Gives users access to live video on the console for all cameras in the site.

**Arm/Disarm Announcement**

Console announces when a site is arming, armed, or disarmed.

**Alarm Trigger Announcement**

Console announces when a site has been tripped.

**Alarm Raised Announcement**

Console announces when an alarm is raised.

**Enable Console Door Chime**

Console plays an audio tone when a door in the site is opened.

**Console Controls**

Restarts the console remotely.

# Cellular Gateway Status LEDs | Connectivity | Verkada Help

Verkada’s [GC31/GC31-E Cellular Gateway](https://www.verkada.com/cellular-gateway)
 is equipped with LED light statuses by model:

**Model**

**Operation Type**

[GC31](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_40806a4487)
 (indoor)

[Regular operation](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_d160696649)

[SIM card operation](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_1f575e66f4)

[GC31-E](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_1394c2a584)
 (outdoor)

[Regular operation](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_b29c15c8c7)

[SIM card operation](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#h_fc60063a6b)

Use this article to learn about the different LED characteristics to help you understand what they mean.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#gc31-status-leds)

GC31 status LEDs


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#regular-operation)

Regular operation

The LED status light consists of the following states:

*   **Solid orange**—GC31 is on and booting up
    
*   **Flashing orange**—GC31 is updating firmware
    
*   **Solid blue**—GC31 is running and online
    
*   **Flashing blue**—GC31 is running and offline
    

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-69e1d4c059601c36100ed37b6b99769d3ffc6ef7%252Fd5b68cd3f90b83812b020f3d35511878586cf2b5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=1614e7b8&sv=2)

### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#sim-card-operation)

SIM card operation

The LED status light consists of the following states:

*   **No light**—No SIM detected
    
*   **Solid white**—SIM card detected
    
*   **Flash white**—SIM card detected and running
    

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-1b056f5a5321a4a0e28562672b174ef042d964c0%252Fabc94f0a57bb547b918af3058f6421e81aeda45b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=b7299674&sv=2)

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#gc31-e-status-leds)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/cellular-gateway-status-leds#regular-operation-1)

# Use Cellular Gateways for WAN Failover | Connectivity | Verkada Help

Cellular Gateways support WAN failover mode, which enables the gateway to act as an uplink to your existing network. In WAN failover mode, the Gateway’s cellular connection will act as a failover, helping ensure that your security devices remain online and operational even when your primary network experiences downtime.

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-df57d7d0a2ca12268ba9b242122d074d8a6c6299%252Fabdede7a2a1bab531cc76f831c98408ac12ededf.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=81ac894f&sv=2)

The cellular connection will remain active when the device is in WAN failover mode and consume minimal data. When the wired ethernet connection fails, the cellular connection acts as a failover, keeping the gateway and any connected devices online.

* * *

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/use-cellular-gateways-for-wan-failover#enable-wan-mode)

Enable WAN mode


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/use-cellular-gateways-for-wan-failover#outdoor-cellular-gateway)

Outdoor Cellular Gateway

WAN failover mode works automatically on the GC31-E.

1

**Plug the ethernet cable into the PoE In port, and the gateway will automatically detect the uplink and use the wired connection.**

2

**Once the gateway receives an IP address from the wired network, a WAN badge will appear on the gateway details page, indicating that the connection was successful and the gateway is now functioning in WAN failover mode.**

3

**Verkada devices need to be connected downstream on the PoE Out port of the cellular gateway and get their IP addresses from the gateway.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-08ce6993b0fb2dea7b9bf48d76f111324963f0f4%252Ff2b8c50262e053b25e06f62c86a12cd72d3be911.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=36e6e1fe&sv=2)

All downstream devices must receive their IP address & DHCP information from the gateway before a WAN failover can occur.

#### 

[](https://help.verkada.com/connectivity/configuration-and-setup/use-cellular-gateways-for-wan-failover#indoor-cellular-gateway)

Indoor Cellular Gateway

To enable WAN failover mode on the GC31, you will need to configure **PoE Out Port 2** to act as an uplink.

1

**In Verkada Command, go to All Products > Gateways .**

2

**Select the gateway you want to configure.**

3

**In the top right, click Settings .**

4

**Under Network > Port 2 Configuration, select Wide Area Network (WAN).**

5

**Click Apply to save the configuration.**

6

**Click Confirm, and the device will reboot. PoE port 2 will now act as a WAN port.**

7

**Plug the ethernet cable into PoE port 2.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-3e0d1178189fa871b6d48aa1b3ad335c5a18be6c%252F3850099f28c5cbb82f4179d014273fbfe1616b41.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=3e80447c&sv=2)

8

**Verkada devices need to be connected downstream on port 1 of the cellular gateway and get their IP addresses from the gateway.**

9

**When the device receives an IP from the wired network, a WAN badge will appear on the gateway details page.**

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F1814166542-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FiAGnzScvko5PkG7YBy3i%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-0ce57203d4c2743f47ba88ee47734a61707566e7%252F981fdb5aa09d4b48643b196fe6fabe44eb67cd3b.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=aad1bbb1&sv=2)

# Set Up Your Wireless Alarm Devices | Classic Alarms | Verkada Help

This article is a guide for classic Alarms. Refer to this [article](https://help.verkada.com/new-alarms/configuration-and-setup/wireless-alarms-devices)
 if you have new Alarms. See [New Alarms vs Classic Alarms](https://help.verkada.com/new-alarms/new-alarms-vs-classic-alarms)
 if you are unsure which version of Alarms you have.

* * *

The Verkada wireless hub and sensors communicate over a proprietary sub-GHz wireless communication protocol. This custom protocol operates at 915 MHz (US, Canada)/868 MHz (UK, EU), and was built from the ground up to maximize security, range, and battery life.

Our wireless signals are encrypted using AES-128. Through direct sequence spread spectrum (DSSS) technology, Verkada’s technology prevents signal jamming and other attacks, which can impact competitor systems.

* * *

![](https://help.verkada.com/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F2326462210-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F9tIFgMOGbY4p9wWaKQhl%252Fuploads%252Fgit-blob-8e8c86fa7a71ac845ea88e0cdbc99a3120b01f3a%252Feeb781bf340e4d66baf9dd64881376ff1907c534.png%3Falt%3Dmedia&width=768&dpr=4&quality=100&sign=99d320d9&sv=2)

[](https://help.verkada.com/classic-alarms/hardware-installation/set-up-your-wireless-alarm-devices#wireless-specs)
